A sample 2-tapes Turing machine to accept the language of all palindromes (strings that read the same from left to right and from right to left) over the alphabet {a, b}: 

let pal : tm2 =
  let d inp =
    match inp with
    | (1, "a", "_") -> (2, "a", 0, "_", 1)
    | (1, "b", "_") -> (2, "b", 0, "_", 1)
    | (1, "_", "_") -> (5, "_", 0, "_", 0)
    | (2, "a", "_") -> (2, "a", 1, "a", 1)
    | (2, "b", "_") -> (2, "b", 1, "b", 1)
    | (2, "_", "_") -> (3, "_", 0, "_", -1)
    | (3, "_", "a") -> (3, "_", 0, "a", -1)
    | (3, "_", "b") -> (3, "_", 0, "b", -1)
    | (3, "_", "_") -> (4, "_", -1, "_", 1)
    | (4, "a", "a") -> (4, "a", -1, "a", 1)
    | (4, "b", "b") -> (4, "b", -1, "b", 1)
    | (4, "a", "_") -> (100, "a", 0, "_", 0)
    | (4, "b", "_") -> (100, "b", 0, "_", 0)
    | _ -> (200, "_", 0, "_", 0) in
  {
    states2 = [1; 2; 3; 4; 100; 200];
    input_alphabet2 = ["a"; "b"];
    tape_alphabet2 = ["a"; "b"; "_"];
    delta2 = d;
    start2 = 1;
    accept2 = 100;
    reject2 = 200;
  }

It uses the obvious generalization of Turing machines that we used in Homework 4. It works by copying the input string on the second tape, then scanning through the string on the first tape from right to left at the same time as scanning the string on the second tape from left to right, transitioning only when the symbols on the two tapes agree.

When converted to a single tape Turing machine through the translation I (badly) described in class, we get a 557 states Turing machine! Here's that Turing machine working to accept the palindrome abbaabba, using an implementation of Turing machines that lets you name states with strings instead of just integers:
